<div id="review_406061639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/406061639" />
    <a title="Alexis *Reality Bites*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5587514-alexis-reality-bites"><img alt="Alexis *Reality Bites*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404308282p2/5587514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/406061639?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexis *Reality Bites*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexis *Reality Bites*" href="/user/show/5587514-alexis-reality-bites">Alexis *Reality Bites*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lovers of Thoughtless by S.C.Stephens and Beautiful Disaster by Jaime McGuire</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5587514-alexis-reality-bites?shelf=new-adult-college">new-adult-college</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer406061639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer569702224237054262">Spoiler Free Review <br/>3.5 to 4 STARS out of 5<br/>Genre: YA/New Adult-Mature content<br/><br/><b>Passengers please lower your harness and fasten your seatbelts for safety. This book hits sharp turns has high peaks and fast drops.<br/>**smiles** <i>Please enjoy the ride!</i></b><br/>Emotional Roller-Coaster does not even begin to describe this book. My face leaked from every hole it has I'm talkin can't stop cryin nose blowin mouth drooling weeping. YES it is that intense. Don't say I didn't warn you.<br/><br/><i>'I wanted to have dysfunctional rela</i></span>
  <span id="freeText569702224237054262" style="display:none">Spoiler Free Review <br />3.5 to 4 STARS out of 5<br />Genre: YA/New Adult-Mature content<br /><br /><b>Passengers please lower your harness and fasten your seatbelts for safety. This book hits sharp turns has high peaks and fast drops.<br />**smiles** <i>Please enjoy the ride!</i></b><br />Emotional Roller-Coaster does not even begin to describe this book. My face leaked from every hole it has I'm talkin can't stop cryin nose blowin mouth drooling weeping. YES it is that intense. Don't say I didn't warn you.<br /><br /><i>'I wanted to have dysfunctional relationships and flings but did that happen? Nope. I felt like Elena from the Vampire Diaries. She has two insanely hot men who are in love with her and would do anything for her. One of which, she would give almost everything to be with, and the other she continues to push away, even though she can't ever actually stay away, so she won't have to admit she was in love with him too. At least my guys weren't brothers. Thank God for that.'</i> <br />-Harpers inner monologue in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15739018.Taking_Chances__Taking_Chances___1_" title="Taking Chances (Taking Chances, #1) by Molly McAdams" rel="nofollow noopener">Taking Chances</a><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Dear God make me a bird so I can fly far far away</i>
</b><br />After eighteen years of growing up under the strict rule of her Marine father properly titled 'Sir.' Harper is finally breaking free. She is now on her way to college clear across the country from North Carolina to the sunshine state. San Diego California. Harper is described by one character as being pure as the snow. She has never had a boyfriend and has never been kissed. AT EIGHTEEN! **Throws hands in the air** <br />Unbelievable right?!<br /> After unpacking she takes a nap. She is later woken up by her procacious roomate Breanna. She tells Harper that her brother is having a party at his house and they will be in attendance. After ruling out <b>everything</b> in Harper's wardrobe Breanna decides they need to hit the mall.<br /><br />The two girls bond quickly and Harper has a hidden crush on Chase; Breanna's brother. Chase is tall blonde with surfer boy hair and piercing blue eyes. He also has a few tattoos. But the guy is a player. Everytime she sees him he is sporting a new chick on his arm lap or wherever else they can hang off him at. <br />Then she meets Brandon one of Chase's many roomates. Brandon is tall with a buzzed cut and sports a cute dimple in his cheek when he smiles. OH and he is also tatted up. When Brandon returns his interest in Harper Chase decides he is not feeling it so he tries to run interference. He knows he is not good for her and as far as he is concerned neither is Brandon. Unfortunately the choice is not his. Harper is not having it and she let's Chase know that she can do what she wants. <i>Then she goes and does exactly that.</i><br /><br />Now this is just the first 11% of the book... <br /><br />After that you will be taken on an emotional ride as Harper becomes torn in between these two guys. She experiences heartbreak and she hands out heartbreak to not one, not two, but three guys.<br /><br /><b>-Cheating takes her from one guy<br /><br />-And lies take one from her</b><br /><br /><i>She lost one. Lose some to Win some, right?!?</i><br /><br /><u>Thoughts</u><br />In all honesty I am a BIG mixed bag of emotions with this book... This is mainly due to the fact that I have a love/hate thing for the heroine Harper. At times I could not stand her. Sorry correction most times I could not stand her. The guys in this book allowed me to enjoy it their witty banter and alpha ways got me all hot and bothered in the best of ways.<br />Also the author did an amazing job with showing the importance of family and friendship. I loved the parts that showcased the family ties the most.<br />If you loved Thoughtless by S.C.Stephens and/or Beautiful Disaster by Jamie McGuire then you should enjoy this book. Just make sure you have the kleenex handy. But no worries twice out of the three times i cried they were happy tears.<br /><br />My Ratings<br />Characters- Lovable except Harper<br />Writing Style- Good<br />Plot/Storyline- Good<br />Steam Factor- Medium/Moderately Steamy<br />Overall- I liked it!!!<br /><br /><b>Now go forth and Read. Then tell us all about it on Goodreads!</b></span>

<div id="review_406128927" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/406128927" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/406128927?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=with-smut">with-smut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=3-neurons-involved">3-neurons-involved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer406128927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer852348111317980774">That I subject myself to stuff like this over and over again can only be definitive proof of my masochistic tendencies. I really don't know why I choose these absurd stories, un-freaking-believable, where the characters are clearly made out of cardboard, where the writing is bad, bad, bad and the editing is worse, where there isn't an original idea even if you look for it with a microscope and which are also about 75% too long than needed. <br/>I kid you not, I was at 30% and had the impression that </span>
  <span id="freeText852348111317980774" style="display:none">That I subject myself to stuff like this over and over again can only be definitive proof of my masochistic tendencies. I really don't know why I choose these absurd stories, un-freaking-believable, where the characters are clearly made out of cardboard, where the writing is bad, bad, bad and the editing is worse, where there isn't an original idea even if you look for it with a microscope and which are also about 75% too long than needed. <br />I kid you not, I was at 30% and had the impression that the story could just as well have wrapped up at that point (as it probably should have).<br />I don't know what to say; I can't, in all honesty, find a redeeming quality in this book. <br />The characterization is appalling: Harper is this absolutely amazing, incredibly beautiful girl who is of course completely unaware of her feminine powers and who goes to college after living with her unloving, completely absent father. He is in the military, a Marine, and she calls him "Sir" (he should have sent her to war, not to college if you ask me and good riddance). Once she gets there, she gets paired up in the dorm with a girl, Breanna, who loves her like crazy from day one and takes her shopping and makes her even more beautiful than she is. Not only that, but she introduces Harper to her friends, who all fall in love with her immediately and who incidentally are these gorgeous, tattooed studs (all six feet three at least). As soon as they see her, they all turn from manwhores to monks, obviously. But that's not all! Even her best friend's parents get so enamored with her that they practically adopt her and have her call them Mom and Dad.<br />Enter the love triangle, which at one point even becomes a square. From there on it's a downward spiral, believe me. I'd like to go more into detail and give you more of a hint of how much this book is messed up but I won't, not to spoil the story for you in the unfortunate case you decide to pick it up. <br /><br />This is a book that lovers of <i>Beautiful Disaster</i> or <i>Thoughtless</i> might appreciate. Maybe. <br />As for the author, I have just one piece of advice: you might want to look up the definition of <i>consecutio temporum</i>. Oh, and apply it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="852348111317980774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_406525989" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/406525989" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/406525989?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=new-adult-college">new-adult-college</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=drama-llama">drama-llama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=frustrating">frustrating</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer406525989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1471186624811843365">Revision 10/07/12 because I laughed my ass off that this new book already made it to number 1 on Listopia's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/list/show/24791.Books_that_seriously_piss_you_off' rel='nofollow noopener'>Books that seriously piss you off</a><br/><blockquote>
  <b>...and <s>Shark</s> Contemporary week rolls on...</b>
</blockquote><br/>I made it a goal before finishing <i>Taking Chances</i> to remain zen for the writing of this review, knowing full well that the last part of the book might set me on edge. Well guess what? <i>I'm perfectly okay.</i><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Look at me, I'm not raging! It's an early Christmas miracle!</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>See, the thing is, the part of the book</span>
  <span id="freeText1471186624811843365" style="display:none">Revision 10/07/12 because I laughed my ass off that this new book already made it to number 1 on Listopia's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/list/show/24791.Books_that_seriously_piss_you_off" rel="nofollow noopener">Books that seriously piss you off</a><br /><blockquote>
  <b>...and <s>Shark</s> Contemporary week rolls on...</b>
</blockquote><br />I made it a goal before finishing <i>Taking Chances</i> to remain zen for the writing of this review, knowing full well that the last part of the book might set me on edge. Well guess what? <i>I'm perfectly okay.</i><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Look at me, I'm not raging! It's an early Christmas miracle!</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />See, the thing is, the part of the book that was supposed to make me angry didn't. It just reminded me of a bad personal memory, so I did a real life frowny face and moved past it. If anything, it wasn't so much that I had a problem with "the incident," it was more that I had a problem with how the incident happened. The incident would have felt more at place within the story without the extra helping of guilt.<br /><br />Btw...writing this review is darn-near impossible. I can't talk about my feelings if I'm not allowed to express why I'm having these feelings. I can't talk about how the various different game changers were hit and miss if I can't list out what they are. <br /><br />Most people who have read this book are pretty much in agreement that the first 2/3 of the book was a great read. I felt the same way. The comparisons to <i>Beautiful Disaster</i> and <i>Thoughtless</i> are semi-warranted but any similarities would be on a much more toned-down scale. If you had a character like Travis who was in control of his feelings and a character like Kellan who was able to keep his eye on the prize, then perhaps we can squint and find a few things in common. But please refer back to the 'toned-down' comment from earlier. One of my biggest complaints about Kiera from <i>Thoughtless</i> was that she let things drag on for far too long. I didn't feel the same way about this book. Eventually, decisions were made before we were stuck on a merry-go-round of bad behavior. <i>I respected that.</i><br /><br /><b>Honestly, even with "the incident," I still probably would have given this book a high score if three things would have been different.</b><br /><br />1. The incident was a product of coincidence and not related to character behavior.<br /><br />2. Harper's decisions had been spread out over a longer period of time. I did not appreciate that she went from one decision to the next and then to the next with no real breathing room in-between. There is this nifty little thing called a chapter heading...we should have been treated to a heading which said <i>One Year Later</i> (after the incident). <br /><br />3. The last 30% of the book was absolutely unnecessary. There's a reason why most books end at the HEA. It's because most of the time people become boring as hell when you see them in their domestic lives. I didn't care to see the majority of what happened after the decision that happened after the incident. I'm all for books about the subject of what happened to Harper (I'll let you off the hook, she did not die in a fire...I know that's what you were guessing), but if that's going to be what happens, then make that the actual book subject...don't advertise it as a book about a love triangle. <br /><br />Random question for those who have read the book : Was there even a reason to have Carter as a character? Love quad? Not really, right?<br /><br /><b>So for my inability to write a review that is anything other than vague, I am awarding <u>Taking Chances</u> first place in the "spoiler difficulty" competition.</b> <br /><br />2 stars is mainly because the book simply dragged on for far too long. I would definitely give something else by this author a shot. I was thoroughly enjoying myself for the first 2/3 of the book. Molly McAdams can sure write extremely <b>likable</b> bad boys. I already touched on this a little bit earlier, but let me go back and clarify : Brandon's ability to hold himself back from turning into a controlling prick did impress me quite a bit. We don't see enough of this in YA, Mature YA, College, and New-Adult fiction. Bravo to that. <br /><br /><b>Between Chase and Brandon, who would I have picked?</b> When I was Harper's age, I would have picked Chase, no question. At the age I'm at now, I'd pick Brandon. Just don't tell Brandon that I was probably swooning harder over Chase.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1471186624811843365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_406213337" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/406213337" />
    <a title="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7379751-gitte-totallybookedblog"><img alt="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514886578p2/7379751.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/406213337?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gitte TotallyBookedBlog" href="/user/show/7379751-gitte-totallybookedblog">Gitte TotallyBookedBlog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7379751-gitte-totallybookedblog?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7379751-gitte-totallybookedblog?shelf=2012-favourites">2012-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer406213337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer532619976171511366">My thoughts on Taking Chances.....<br/><br/>I felt myself being pulled back and forth between Chase and Brandon, I couldn't decide at first but I decided on Brandon, and I have to say he was my choice throughout. And yes, I know I am in the minority! So Harper's actions peeved me off no end!!!!!<br/><br/>However, my thoughts on that is that here's this girl who has been like a bird locked in her cage throughout her life, starved from love with no Mum and a Dad who she respected but had a pretty cold and no affectio</span>
  <span id="freeText532619976171511366" style="display:none">My thoughts on Taking Chances.....<br /><br />I felt myself being pulled back and forth between Chase and Brandon, I couldn't decide at first but I decided on Brandon, and I have to say he was my choice throughout. And yes, I know I am in the minority! So Harper's actions peeved me off no end!!!!!<br /><br />However, my thoughts on that is that here's this girl who has been like a bird locked in her cage throughout her life, starved from love with no Mum and a Dad who she respected but had a pretty cold and no affection relationship with. She had Carter and the other lads, but these were in her mind friendships, not lust/love. She has never experienced the attraction, the longing, the lust or the love. So it hit her over the head when she met these 2 amazing blokes!<br /><br />When she gets to spread her wings, express herself as she wants/likes and receives adoration, protection, love in return she herself loves right back. Brandon and Chase are 2 separate objects of affection and love. I think she falls in love with both because at the end of the day not only are they gorgeous, they both offer her what she has been lacking all her life. Chase just happened to come across her first. That initial meeting sparked something in her which if it hadn't been for his reputation possibly could have changed the whole story. Her defense mechanism was to flee, however he was already in her heart.<br /><br />Harper is one intense and love starved young woman who craves to be loved and love in return. She has so much to give. With Chase however, throughout the story she wanted to protect herself. It is as if she was just waiting for the inevitable to occur, like repeating a mantra of 'he will cheat and leave me loveless'. Brandon on the other hand did not have this reputation, and he loves as hard as Chase, he is almost like the safer option emotionally. I have no doubt though that Chase would have stayed faithful, I am so sure he would have given her everything and never strayed! <br /><br />My heart broke and I actually wanted to vomit when "the thing" happened. Worst scene EVER!! It still breaks my heart and I still now think WTF!!! I hate it, I really do!!<br /><br />I LOVED this ending. But then again I LOVE emotional books and if I cry in a book I know it means I just read a bloody amazing one!!! Although at times I really hated Harper with a passion, I kind of understood her.<br /><br />I know this is fiction, but I also know that stuff like this happens in real life, it really does. People grow up starved of love and they overcompensate subconsciously by loving too much. With sudden freedom comes sudden rebellion against the norm or what is deemed acceptable. But who says it has to be so?!<br /><br />I hated Trish, I wanted to bitch slap her into tomorrow, however, the guilt she has to live with for the rest of her life, well that is enough punishment as well as what Harper dished out!! <br /><br />So yes, I both loved and hated this book but Molly's writing has to be applauded for evoking such extreme emotions!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="532619976171511366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421574402?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421574402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4628449017540817792"><b>We suspend our disbelief, and not our intelligence in reading.</b> So, know that plenty moments in this had me calling BS (never been to a mall, my patootie.) Frankly, I do see why it's well received by some, what with its tatted-up bad boy, secret fighter good boy, and the girl with zero experience... except, as usual, for me, things got a bit <i>much...</i> <br/><br/><b> The <s>story's</s> Drama's Progression:</b> <br/><blockquote>1. Cow eyes from one or two of them directed at her. <br/>2. Love is in the air, and their inner cavemen start coming ou</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText4628449017540817792" style="display:none"><b>We suspend our disbelief, and not our intelligence in reading.</b> So, know that plenty moments in this had me calling BS (never been to a mall, my patootie.) Frankly, I do see why it's well received by some, what with its tatted-up bad boy, secret fighter good boy, and the girl with zero experience... except, as usual, for me, things got a bit <i>much...</i> <br /><br /><b> The <s>story's</s> Drama's Progression:</b> <br /><blockquote>1. Cow eyes from one or two of them directed at her. <br />2. Love is in the air, and their inner cavemen start coming out. <br />3. A text, a message and her jealousies cloud her judgment. <br />4. Cue the waterworks/ walking off/ running out <br />5. Beg for forgiveness from one of them. <br />6. Declarations of love (or of her specialness and of his/their desire of not wanting to hurt her.) <br />7. And, all is well. <br />8. Back to 1 and continue from there.</blockquote> <br />The drama just kept going on and on and on, the escalating sort because the girl was prone to overreacting and not thinking things through… and get this: running away! hardly anyone calls her on it and it got unreal.<br /><br /><b>Drinking Game!</b><br /><blockquote><b>One shot</b> each time she or any one of them says, <i>‘my word’, ‘oh my word’, or ‘dear lord’</i>; <br /><b>Two</b> for each declaration of love/ someone saying they just want to take care of her/ protect her/ love her/ make her his; <br /><b>Three,</b> each time someone says they don’t deserve her.<br /><br />NO, really.. things got old.</blockquote> <br />On the bright side, I did get some unintentional laughs out of this especially with her likening their life to Vampire Diaries (she fancies herself an Elena!) So, one must wonder: why keep at it if nothing was working for me? I honestly don’t know, is it enough that the sexy times were sexy? Sadly, no... at least, not this time around. <br /><br /><b>1/5</b><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17068403261970611240"><b>(THIS CONTAINS HUUUGE SPOILERS)</b><br/><br/>Okay, this is hard. I usually don’t review books that I have given 1 star but on this one, I’m willing to make an exception.<br/><br/>First, I have nothing against the Author. All the reasons I have given this book a 1 star is really just because of the book. Second, It’s not because of the writing. I honestly think it’s okay-written so yeah.. It’s all because of the PLOT!<br/><br/>I have never – EVER – been so disappointed on a book before! SOMEBODY GIVE ME A TROPHY FOR PUNISHING MYS</span>
  <span id="freeText17068403261970611240" style="display:none"><b>(THIS CONTAINS HUUUGE SPOILERS)</b><br><br>Okay, this is hard. I usually don’t review books that I have given 1 star but on this one, I’m willing to make an exception.<br><br>First, I have nothing against the Author. All the reasons I have given this book a 1 star is really just because of the book. Second, It’s not because of the writing. I honestly think it’s okay-written so yeah.. It’s all because of the PLOT!<br><br>I have never – EVER – been so disappointed on a book before! SOMEBODY GIVE ME A TROPHY FOR PUNISHING MYSELF BY FINISHING THIS! I DESERVE IT! The only emotional response I had towards this book was absolute frustration!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455174045ra/18065562.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The story was on Harper’s POV. The first part of the book was great (yes, I actually liked the first part). Harlot, I mean Harper was introduced as the kind of girl with no experience (at all) of partying and boys because she’s homeschooled.</b>She grew up with a bunch of young marines and her dad whom she calls ‘Sir’. So when she decides to go to college at San Diego State University to escape her life, she immediately became a wild party girl with the help of her roommate, who is also the one who introduced Harper to her brother, Chase (a fighter with tats). <b>Harper also got introduced to Brandon (also a fighter). AND THIS IS WHERE THE STORY STARTS TO BECOME A TOTAL CRAP.</b><br><br><b>Harper was now suddenly torn between Chase and her boyfriend Brandon. Harper the harlot cheated on her boyfriend by having sex with Chase (TWICE!) without even using protection. Because she’s smart like that. Ladies and Gents(?), wanna guess what’s the result of that? HARPER ENDS UP PREGNANT with Chase’s child! Of course she was shocked and sickened and oh my god she don’t what to do.. Anybody want to slap and laugh at her face? I DO!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455174045ra/18065563.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I’m going to give Harper a highlight on this review because she’s the sole reason why I hated this book with passion.<b> She was so efffing annoying! At any chapter, I was ready to jump inside the book and strangle her.<br><br><b>WHAT’S WRONG WITH YOU?!</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455174045ra/18065564.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455174045ra/18065565.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, now that that part is done let us get through with this. <b>Harper and Chase decided to live together because of their child and of course I have to endure those moments when she’ll get jealous because there are girls who’s trying to steal her maaaan. She even caught Chase with another women on bed and she was raging with anger!! ARE YOU KIDDING ME?!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455174045ra/18065566.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>DIDN’T YOU CHEAT ON BRANDON AND DIDN’T EVEN FEEL ANY GUILT?! WOW HARPER YOU DESERVE THE 'I-AM-THE-BEST-HYPOCRITE’ AWARD. HERE TAKE IT</b><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455174045ra/18065567.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>THEEEN the crappiest thing happened, Chase dies… he was hit by a truck or something on his way to harper to prove that he’s not cheating.</b><br><br><b>I’M SO SAD, CAN YOU SEE THE SINGLE TEAR ON MY EYE?</b><br> <br><b>The story continues after Chase death and guess where Harper ran to? Yep, BRANDON! You would think that Harper would just lay low and take care of her baby for a while because of Chase, but NOOOOOO.</b> Harper the harlot is on the move again and she ended up marrying Brandon. All through out she was just thinking that Chase would’ve wanted her decision. That it’s what Chase would’ve wanted.<br><br><b>WELL OF COURSE HARPER, CHASE WANTED YOU TO MARRY AS SOON AS HE DIES. DON’T GRIEVE HIM, I MEAN HE’S JUST THE FATHER OF YOUR CHILD RIGHT?! NICE SEEING THAT YOU CARED ABOUT CHASE.</b><br><br>After two months, Harper moved in to Brandon’s because of The dysfunctional family that convinced her. UGH- don’t even get me started by the family. I just want to slap them all. Harper got pregnant again with Brandon’s child (Ah yes, let’s all give her a pat on the back for not cheating) and now the children ended up calling Chase… UNCLE CHASE!!!!!! NOW THAT’S JUST WRONG!<br><br><br><b>HE IS ONE OF THE FATHER FOR PETE’S SAKE!</b><br><br>Seriously this book is driving me crazy.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455174045ra/18065568.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>Now let me just wrap this up now.. TAKING CHANCES is a big fat mess! This book really angered me to the point that I questioned myself 'WHAT THE HELL IS WRONG WITH YOU AND WHY DID YOU READ IT?’ This book drove me nuts. Harper the harlot is one of the most unlikeable heroine ever! She’s a whiny brat. (let me just think of more synonyms for annoying) I hate her for making females look dumb!<br><br>Author, how can you write a character like that? WHYYYY?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455174045ra/18065569.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So why did I gave it 1 star again? Because this book deserves it! Should you read it?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455174045ra/18065570.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b></b></span>

<div id="review_407227415" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/407227415" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572125481p2/3283298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/407227415?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nobody. Stay away.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=24-ebooks">24-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=05-crush-worthy-guy">05-crush-worthy-guy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=25-hawt">25-hawt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=08-dnf">08-dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=03-hall-of-shame">03-hall-of-shame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=32-made-me-want-to-pull-my-hair-out">32-made-me-want-to-pull-my-hair-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=33-college-romance">33-college-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3283298-jessica?shelf=34-contemporary-new-adult">34-contemporary-new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer407227415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12187349856684143003">It’s not like I haven’t been warned. There are plenty of reviews out there telling people just how <b>DRAMATIC</b> this story is. Yet, I couldn’t stay away...I just <i>had</i> to find out for myself. Well, what do they say? Curiosity killed the cat.<br/><br/>What.The.F*ck. Seriously.<br/><br/>You know, I started off liking this story. I have a thing for cocky bad boys and there were some pretty steamy scenes and so I thought this would be right up my alley. WRONG! Things got ridiculous pretty quickly after basically the entire m</span>
  <span id="freeText12187349856684143003" style="display:none">It’s not like I haven’t been warned. There are plenty of reviews out there telling people just how <b>DRAMATIC</b> this story is. Yet, I couldn’t stay away...I just <i>had</i> to find out for myself. Well, what do they say? Curiosity killed the cat.<br /><br />What.The.F*ck. Seriously.<br /><br />You know, I started off liking this story. I have a thing for cocky bad boys and there were some pretty steamy scenes and so I thought this would be right up my alley. WRONG! Things got ridiculous pretty quickly after basically the entire male population (including said bad boy) started to fall all over themselves to take care of Harper, declaring their absolute admiration and undying love for her. <i>Because there’s just something about her, ya know?</i> *eye roll* <br /><br />With this book everything was just too much, totally overdone and painfully melodramatic.<br /><br />So I’m going to do myself a favor and stop reading at 65% into the story because I’m just too exasperated with this story, the characters and the author. Now I hope my eye’s gonna stop twitching soon.<br /><br />Oh, and if you're planning on reading this anyway? Make sure you're not getting invested in any of the characters because that will come back to bite you.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12187349856684143003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13789905922487672904" style="display:none">If you had asked me for a star rating at around the 50% mark of this book I would have said 5 big shiny stars because up to this point all I had done since picking up the book was ; <br><br><img height="263" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/538660.gif" width="220" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved it, I was gripped, I couldn't put it down, I had to force myself to put my ipad down just to carry out basic daily functions....wow what a book.......<br><br>But then I readjust passed the 50% mark and a certain event happens and I was like; <br><br><img height="190" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/518111.gif" width="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img height="183" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/371294.gif" width="245" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then I carried on reading and I was like;<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403431ra/784868.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then I couldn't help but feel like;<br><br><img alt="image" height="233" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403431ra/784869.gif" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then I kept on reading and reading and reading and I'm sorry to say but it got a little;<br><br><img height="237" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403431ra/784870.gif" width="500" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So then I got to the end and I was like;<br><br><img alt="image" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403431ra/784871.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And if you asked me for a rating at this point I would probably have said 2 stars......so now I just don't know. <br><br>This was such a Jekyll and Hyde book for me.   <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_408275328" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/408275328" />
    <a title="Natasha is a Book Junkie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie"><img alt="Natasha is a Book Junkie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585046882p2/9389992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/408275328?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha is a Book Junkie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha is a Book Junkie" href="/user/show/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie">Natasha is a Book Junkie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer408275328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7471766894750813843">When a book decides to tackle such serious topics such as this one, I feel that a review has to reflect that. It would be irresponsible and quite out of character for me to just skim over the massive elephant in the room and focus only on how un-puttable-down this story might have been or how pleasantly angsty some parts of it were. This is a serious book, this is not a book for the light-hearted and this is not an easy read. The best way I can describe the way the events in this book affected m</span>
  <span id="freeText7471766894750813843" style="display:none">When a book decides to tackle such serious topics such as this one, I feel that a review has to reflect that. It would be irresponsible and quite out of character for me to just skim over the massive elephant in the room and focus only on how un-puttable-down this story might have been or how pleasantly angsty some parts of it were. This is a serious book, this is not a book for the light-hearted and this is not an easy read. The best way I can describe the way the events in this book affected me would be to compare it to a wash cycle - starts slow, gentle, gradually picks up in pace, faster and faster but still safe and pain-free, then all of a sudden it starts throwing your heart around savagely and with no warning, you find yourself in a spin cycle, not knowing which way is up, and then the pace slows down again, stays slow, attempts to mend your devastated heart, but in the end you can never forget the experience of having been through that spin cycle.<br /><br />This is the story of a young girl, Harper, raised and home-schooled at a military base until she was eighteen by a strict father who treated her the same way he treated his Marines - with detachment and free from emotions. Surrounded only by males throughout her entire childhood, Harper grows up with no female influences in her life. When she starts college, she finds herself not only away from home for the first time in her life, but also in an environment as foreign to her as it is exciting. She craves to find herself and catch up on all the experiences that she has missed out on while growing up.<br /><blockquote>
  <em>“After eighteen years of struggling to achieve a perfection that couldn’t be reached in my father’s eyes, I was finally going to let loose, have the college experience - whatever that was - and hopefully find out who I am in the process.”</em>
</blockquote><br />She quickly finds herself surrounded by new friends, free to do whatever she chooses to do, left to her own inexperienced devices. But what happens when you let an animal that has lived in captivity for almost two decades, free? It runs, it embraces freedom never thinking of consequences, it takes risks and it makes mistakes. Add to that the emotional immaturity of an eighteen-year-old girl and you’ve got the perfect formula for disaster. Harper finds herself in a delicious little love triangle within a week of her new college life, with no prior experience in matters of the heart or being the object of anyone’s affection. Enter Chase and Brandon, equally scrumptious and equally exciting as potential love candidates for our virginal heroine, but different as night and day.<br /><br />Chase is the archetypal rebel-without-a-cause, a ‘bad boy’ whose longest relationship with a girl has barely lasted until the following morning. Meeting Harper changes something in him - he teases her relentlessly and does everything to repel her but he only does so because he sees himself as unworthy of someone like her.<br /><blockquote>
  <em>“I don’t deserve you either. You need someone who will cherish you, protect you and take care of you. Someone that realizes they’d never be able to find another you in the world, no matter how hard they looked. ... That first night, I did realize I would never meet another girl like you. But you deserve someone who has waited for you as long as you have waited for them. And no matter how much I wish I could be that guy, I can’t ... You’re amazing Harper. There will never be anyone good enough for you.”</em>
</blockquote><br />Their attraction is mutual and equally strong but ultimately fruitless once she meets Brandon. He is the perfect guy for Harper. He is demonstrative, open, affectionate and he doesn’t play games with her. Their attraction is just as strong and it quickly evolves into a proper relationship. Harper’s heart is torn in two, she loves both Chase and Brandon but she only sees a future with one of them.<br /><blockquote>
  <em>“I don’t want to be just another girl to someone ...”</em>
</blockquote><br />Prepare yourself for a very angsty and very bumpy ride at this point, the culmination being a mistake that can’t be corrected or pretend it never happened, and everything changes after that. Harper quickly learns the meaning of heartache, how painful the consequences of her actions can be and how to be a responsible adult. I admired her for the decisions she made at that point but some of her reasoning behind it drove me bananas.<br /><br />And then the 'spin cycle' starts - with no warning or indication that the story would take that turn - and I was left breathless for a while, gasping for air, wishing I misread or misinterpreted sentences, hoping it was just a tasteless joke at my expense. I hated the sudden turn of events, I hated that the author thought this would have been an acceptable way of dealing with the love triangle situation and I think I never forgave her for it. I personally felt that the shock-effect was unnecessary and that the gravity of the event affected my enjoyment of the rest of the book. It didn’t make the story any more ‘real’ or poignant, it just made it cruelly heartbreaking.<br /><br />The pace of the second half of the book, 'post-spin cycle', stood in stark contrast to the first half of it. I almost felt it was written by two different people. The dialogues were unnatural, forced at times, and it didn’t flow well for me. When you break your reader’s heart with an unexpected event you have to make sure that you don’t break their spirit as well and that is where this book failed me as a reader. The subsequent events did very little to soothe me, to heal or restore my faith in the story itself. I feel that if you serve a grave injustice to the reader as part of the storyline and know for a fact that it will devastate them, you must also eventually offer an equally important ‘gift’ in return, some sort of redemption to make sense of the suffering. There has to be a balance between ‘good’ and ‘bad’ events and I felt that the scales were dramatically overturned in favour of the bad, for nothing else but the shock value of it. I admit that once the story changed, the characters changed as well, it modified the dynamic between them, it taught them to value what is truly important in life but some of those things could have been achieved differently. I also found that the second part of the book was so ‘detail-heavy’, every single thing was spelled out, from the way a child’s dirty onesie is washed from cake and frosting to how often a child is breastfed during the night and who gets up when he cries. It was unnecessary and apart from confusing me and making me wonder why I needed to know all those details, it added very little to the development of the characters or the plot itself.<br /><blockquote>
  <em>“That boy was covered in cake and frosting. I took his onesie off and rinsed it off in the sink so all the food was [to] go down the drain instead of the washer, then helped ... attempt to wipe him down. We gave up not even two minutes later and ... rushed to give him a bath and put him in new clothes.”</em>
</blockquote><br />I’ll be the first one to admit that I seek angst in my books, I need the cathartic effect that they offer me and I love nothing more than a well-executed emotional roller-coaster. But I do not like having my heart bulldozered and left for dead in the process without even being told the reason for it. The ‘lessons leant’ did not outweigh the 'price paid' and I was left flat, confused, resentful. However, regardless of how I felt at the end of this book, this is a story about the fragility of life itself, about what truly constitutes ‘family’ and about second chances. If you feel like you can erect a bullet-proof wall around your heart and take this book at face value without questioning the necessity of some of its parts, then you will undoubtedly enjoy it.<br /><blockquote>
  <em>“People mess up and make mistakes all the time. Everyone deserves a second chance, right?”</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />~ N ♥<br /><br /><a href="http://wp.me/p2AtqW-ig" rel="nofollow noopener">See this review on my blog!</a> | <a href="http://www.facebook.com/natashaisabookjunkie" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow me on Facebook!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7471766894750813843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer414071269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15801261822548381277">Being a big fan of Beautiful Disaster and Thoughtless/Effortless, I'm always looking for a book that will give me the same adrenaline rush I felt when I read those. Taking Chances was that book for me. It has the incredibly sexy, tatted, buzzed-head hero who makes a living as an underground fighter like BD and the heart-wrenching love triangle between a sweet girl and two equally awesome frat brothers who are both in love with her like T/E. Can Romancelandia get any better for me? Not likely.<br/><br/>Har</span>
  <span id="freeText15801261822548381277" style="display:none">Being a big fan of Beautiful Disaster and Thoughtless/Effortless, I'm always looking for a book that will give me the same adrenaline rush I felt when I read those. Taking Chances was that book for me. It has the incredibly sexy, tatted, buzzed-head hero who makes a living as an underground fighter like BD and the heart-wrenching love triangle between a sweet girl and two equally awesome frat brothers who are both in love with her like T/E. Can Romancelandia get any better for me? Not likely.<br><br>Harper Jackson has just started her freshman year at San Diego State University. Being raised by a strict, emotionless father on a military base in North Carolina, she is completely overwhelmed by her over-zealous roommate Bree and the craziness of living in the dorms on campus. Bree's brother, Chase, is the first guy she meets; and, although they fall into a routine of trading snarky remarks with each other, Chase's chiseled, tatted body and surfer good looks have Harper secretly swooning despite her vow to steer clear of the obvious "man-ho". But then she meets Brandon, the sexy "Travis Maddox look-alike" and it is love at first sight for both of them. Unfortunately, Brandon lives in Chase's frat house and it becomes a messy love triangle that escalates to disastrous proportions.<br><br>I can't say anything more in detail without giving away the story, but it is an amazing, heart-wrenching, soul-searching journey that Harper embarks upon in her first year of college. It is a long book - just short of 500 pages - but I was so caught up in Harper's dilemma with her two awesome men that I read the book in one sitting. Yes, it is that good!<br><br>This is Molly McAdams debut "new adult" novel and I'm excited for her to write more because she has that special "gift" of bringing her characters alive and making her readers feel as though we know these people personally. I wholeheartedly recommend this book to all lovers of a good romance but especially to those who are still in a state of limbo after experiencing Travis Maddox and Kellan Kyle. But heed this warning: Have a box of tissue handy...there are a few situations that will have you tearing up and one incident that will tear your heart to pieces! *sniff*<br><br>5+ stars!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391168i/753314.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Chase<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391168i/753315.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Brandon</span>

  <span id="freeText6797652119400087320" style="display:none"><br><br><b>***DNF***</b><br><br>Ok, I have been refraining from rating or reviewing DNF books but I am not going to do it anymore. <div id="review_531930510" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/531930510" />
    <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads"><img alt="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380942477p2/4197769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/531930510?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline&#39;s Reads" href="/user/show/4197769-jacqueline-s-reads">Jacqueline&#39;s Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jacqueline's Reads by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/11902534-mandee-migliaccio">Mandee Migliaccio</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer531930510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6242745648736770964"><a href='http://imgur.com/LIXiWLp' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409012i/800559._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>4 Dramatic Stars</b><br/><br/>This will be a hard review for me because there are a lot of elements in Taking Chances I have personal issues with. So please note, these are personal issues and this is my personal opinion.<br/><br/><b>Here we go…</b><br/><br/>A lot of people recommended Taking Chances to me. However, my girlfriend read it and DNF. I asked her why and she basically told me what happened up until the 50% mark. So I have been putting it off for a very long time. I don’t know why I decided to pick up, maybe because I am</span>
  <span id="freeText6242745648736770964" style="display:none"><a href="http://imgur.com/LIXiWLp" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409012i/800559._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>4 Dramatic Stars</b><br><br>This will be a hard review for me because there are a lot of elements in Taking Chances I have personal issues with. So please note, these are personal issues and this is my personal opinion.<br><br><b>Here we go…</b><br><br>A lot of people recommended Taking Chances to me. However, my girlfriend read it and DNF. I asked her why and she basically told me what happened up until the 50% mark. So I have been putting it off for a very long time. I don’t know why I decided to pick up, maybe because I am a masochist or my morbid curiosity? What-ever the reason, I needed to know what happens in the end.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/I3EREaI" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409012i/800560.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Taking Chances is not a typical book. It’s not cookie cutter, it’s raw, it’s emotional and you will make you cry like a baby. No, there’s not a “chance” you will cry, it’s a definite, 100% you will need tissues and valium to finish reading.<br><br><b>Seriously...</b><br><a href="http://imgur.com/hqGn0G6" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380409012ra/800561.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Taking Chances is about Harper, the Heroine and two Heroes, Chase and Brandon. This is their love story. It’s not typical, but sometimes shit <br>happens.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/QCEjTwv" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380409012ra/800562.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Let’s get my first issue out, I do not like love triangles when it’s between an indecisive girl and two great Heroes. I need one of the Heroes to be a villain and I didn’t get that. You will fall in love with both men. Chase is the bad-boy player and Brandon is the perfect bring-him-home-meet-the-parents kind of guy. I wavered between Chase and Brandon throughout the read. I couldn’t pin-point who I wanted more and Harper didn’t make it any easier.<br><br><b>
  <u>This is where my review will become spoiler-ish.</u>
</b> I will not give away the main event, but I have to point this out because I do not like this issue. So, do not continue to read if you want a spoiler-free review.<br><br><br><b>I do not like cheating.</b> <br><br>I hardly like a book that has cheating, it’s very rare and when I realized this is pure bluntly cheating, I cringed … major. I have to like the Heroine in some aspects and I just didn’t understand Harper or her issues. I felt like she was just having the best of both worlds. I couldn’t relate.<br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/NuVSiY0" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409012i/800563.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And there is the “EVENT” as I like to call it. I knew about this, I was waiting for it throughout the read and I didn’t realize it would be at the 60% mark before I got there and oh boy, even though I was prepared, it just gutted me. I couldn’t comprehend the shift in the book. I was thinking there has to be a reason why it’s going in this direction, HAS.TO.BE.<br><br><b>Again, seriously... My emotions towards the read...</b><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/h2qSUqQ" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380409012ra/800564.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/kX9PBk9" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380409012ra/800565.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://imgur.com/eYoEjXM" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380409012ra/800566.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The rest of the 40% is cleaning up and when I got to the ending, I was left waiting for something more, like a climatic-ending.<br><br>I gave Taking Chances 4 stars because I’ll give Molly props for a dramatic story, despite my issues. I did find some parts dragging and the story a bit long. I think if she had the “event” at the 30% mark, made Harper a little less wishy-washy, cut out about 100 pages and gave me a dramatic ending, this could have been easily a 5 star read. I get the rave reviews and I get the disappointed ones. I feel like I’m in the middle.<br><br>I haven’t decided if I want to read Stealing Harper, but for now it’s on my list and I will continue to read McAdam’s reads.<br><br>For more reviews, visit <a href="http://jacquelinesreads.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Jacqueline's Reads</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6242745648736770964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText18411284437679620473" style="display:none">What a freaking mess!!!! What in the hell was I thinking picking this book?!<br>If the previous one I read didn't stir up any emotion, this one is the complete opposite. <br><br>Long story short, there's this eighteen-year-old girl, who moves across country to start college, away from Sir (her very strict and detached single Army dad). So there you have it. <b>A HUGE FREAKING MESS!</b> <br><br>Most part of the book I was like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460462442ra/18743554.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>and<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1503828704ra/23696566.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>and<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473045341ra/20394207.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This book is the definition of love triangles.   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/406838747" />
    <a title="Sara " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5058304-sara"><img alt="Sara " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1439650883p2/5058304.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/406838747?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara " href="/user/show/5058304-sara">Sara </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=angst">angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=intense">intense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=hot-tattooed-male">hot-tattooed-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5058304-sara?shelf=kleenex-worthy">kleenex-worthy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer406838747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1491749755579134966">***<b>REVIEW EDIT: 9/17/2012 Contains Spoilers:</b><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>This will be the first time I have done this, drop a book rating after I posted my original review. My reason for this; I cannot let this story go and not in a good way at all. I keep thinking about the first half of the book compared to the second half. I LOVED the first half, loved the dynamics between Chase and Harper and even Harper and Brandon. I was prepared for the angst of the story and the emotional ride of what would happen with this love tri</span>
  <span id="freeText1491749755579134966" style="display:none">***<b>REVIEW EDIT: 9/17/2012 Contains Spoilers:</b><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />This will be the first time I have done this, drop a book rating after I posted my original review. My reason for this; I cannot let this story go and not in a good way at all. I keep thinking about the first half of the book compared to the second half. I LOVED the first half, loved the dynamics between Chase and Harper and even Harper and Brandon. I was prepared for the angst of the story and the emotional ride of what would happen with this love triangle and who would get the love of this young girl. <br /><br />The more I think about what happened I just can't leave the book with my original rating. I can't let go of the fact that Chase died; he didn't just die to me he felt murdered. Not just the physical being in the story but his memory entirely! It seemed after he died that everyone just turned to Brandon as a replacement. Not just Harper, but Chase's own family just brushed the fact that he was gone aside and "Brandon you are like a son to us" blah blah blah. I absolutely hate the fact that it is mentioned that Liam looks nothing like his father. If you kill off this character who leaves behind a child, this kid should be the IMAGE of Chase! Ugh. Harper find her engagement ring and can't deal with it. What about saving the ring for your son to give to his fiance when he gets older. Maybe have a piece of his father. <br /><br />Like, I said. I have never done this before but I can't let it go. I respect the author for trying something new but the angst and emotion I felt in the beginning of the book was lost once we lost Chase. I understand Brandon was the good guy but the end was too sweet, too perfect and just too wrong for me. <br /><br /><br /><br /><b>***Original REVIEW, September 8, 2012***</b><br />So waiting for the release of another book I decided I need a love triangle angst filled story fix. Low and behold Taking Chances was <b>ALL</b> over Goodreads so I checked it out. <br /><br /><i>Cover:</i> <b>LOVE IT</b><br /><i>Synopsis:</i> <b>WTH? Here I come!</b><br /><br />I dove right in expecting the angst of the story and what I got was so much more. MUCH MORE! <br /><br />It will be hard to review this without giving away what needs to be revealed only when you read it for yourself. <br /><br />This story is an emotional roller coaster that has some really tough parts to read. I had to literally put my Nook down and walk away from the story so I could pull myself together and continue reading. <br /><br />The first half of this story moves like lighting and then it tapers off. It is perfect for the story telling; you need that chaos in the beginning to become emotionally invested with the characters and to get in Harper's head and you do. I was so confused and conflicted right along with her. <br /><br />I will put a disclaimer on this book; if you are an emotional reader like myself, have tissues handy and someone to text or call for support. I was lucky I had that with a friend and some gals here on Goodreads as well as a short note from the author. By the way Molly, you need to figure out how to virtually send the wine and ice cream! <br /><br />Taking Chances is aptly named for all the characters in the story do just that. Taking a chance and not knowing the outcome of your actions whether good or bad is what breathes life into our lives. <br /><br />For me this quote is perfect for this story: <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"No matter how much I want it, I can't ask for a future with you because of what I did, it would be selfish."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Review posted at: <a href="http://therisqueredheadreads.com/?p=343&amp;preview=true" rel="nofollow noopener">The Risqué Redhead Reads</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1491749755579134966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_406838821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/406838821" />
    <a title="Jenny - TotallybookedBlog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3870376-jenny---totallybookedblog"><img alt="Jenny - TotallybookedBlog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554795448p2/3870376.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/406838821?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny - TotallybookedBlog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny - TotallybookedBlog" href="/user/show/3870376-jenny---totallybookedblog">Jenny - TotallybookedBlog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer406838821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14518770202333385600">I am so conflicted about this book. I've spent the last couple of days trying to work out how I felt.<br/><br/>The reason I'm conflicted is because even though I didn't love this book, I also couldn't put this it down and just HAD to keep reading.<br/><br/>I figure there must have been something about it that made me continue because the heroine Harper drove me crazy. So much so that any emotion I should have felt was squelched by my dislike for her because, quite frankly, she annoyed the hell out of me.<br/><br/>I really di</span>
  <span id="freeText14518770202333385600" style="display:none">I am so conflicted about this book. I've spent the last couple of days trying to work out how I felt.<br /><br />The reason I'm conflicted is because even though I didn't love this book, I also couldn't put this it down and just HAD to keep reading.<br /><br />I figure there must have been something about it that made me continue because the heroine Harper drove me crazy. So much so that any emotion I should have felt was squelched by my dislike for her because, quite frankly, she annoyed the hell out of me.<br /><br />I really didn't understand how everyone this girl came into contact with fell instantly in love with her. Based on her character and what I read, I just didn't get it.<br /><br />I think I'm a minority on my feelings for this book - I just didn't feel the emotion everyone is feeling and trust me....anyone that knows me, knows I cry at the drop of a hat if a book hits me emotionally.<br /><br />For some reason I felt anger at the twist. I definitely didn't see it coming and it hit me for six, so absolute kudo's to the author for that.<br /><br />I think my issue was that I'm a person who likes to make up my own mind about which "guy team" I choose. I don't like to be "pushed" into a decision and herein lies the problem for me. I felt the author forced me onto another team and for that reason I didn't feel what I should have felt. Maybe I was too invested the other way.<br /><br />I liked the first half of this book but have to say, once the twist happened, it felt like I was sort of going through the motions. I didn't feel connected to the characters after that.<br /><br />The similarity between Beautiful Disaster and Thoughtless was quite obvious to me. I understand that a book might have a similar "feel" to another book. It happens a lot, but there were times during the first half of this book I had to do a double take. The tattooed MMA Underground fighter who gets a call at the last minute to attend a fight at College was really similar to BD for me. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14518770202333385600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZpFb2gfvOFCxrok//8kSZryH+F3rVrjrZ+qL/d0ZI8JctzIIvLHxOBaFPV4IPBi5atgflSXbNow8lM1MEFrRWA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Uzc0nnXMXGELvp///zXS11LQlNIGinVeYjaDEepfiBxpEV1MzpKVCayVK54IwNgIhI9zGsgH+zk5SMWgJxx6hg==')})
  }
//]]>
